# A Survey of Automatic Evaluation Methods on Text, Visual and Speech Generations

(2018; 20 February 2007; 12 March 2009; 5 June 2009)

###### Abstract.

Recent advances in deep learning have significantly enhanced generative AI capabilities across text, images, and audio. However, automatically evaluating the quality of these generated outputs presents ongoing challenges. Although numerous automatic evaluation methods exist, current research lacks a systematic framework that comprehensively organizes these methods across text, visual, and audio modalities. To address this issue, we present a comprehensive review and a unified taxonomy of automatic evaluation methods for generated content across all three modalities; We identify five fundamental paradigms that characterize existing evaluation approaches across these domains. Our analysis begins by examining evaluation methods for text generation, where techniques are most mature. We then extend this framework to image and audio generation, demonstrating its broad applicability. Finally, we discuss promising directions for future research in cross-modal evaluation methodologies.

## 1. Introduction

Deep learning technologies have advanced significantly in recent years, driving major progress in generative models across various domains and tasks (OpenAI et al., [2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib278); Tu et al., [2025b](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib382); Liu et al., [2024k](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib228); Rombach et al., [2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib318); Zhang et al., [2023e](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib480); Tu et al., [2025a](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib378)). Large language models (LLMs) such as GPT-4 and Claude now generate remarkably human-like conversations (OpenAI et al., [2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib278)), while diffusion models (Ho et al., [2020](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib106); Sun et al., [2024d](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib358); Rombach et al., [2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib318); Sun et al., [2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib356); Podell et al., [2023](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib296); Sun et al., [2024e](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib357)) like DALL-E and Stable Diffusion (Rombach et al., [2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib318)) have transformed image and video synthesis. This rapid development raises a critical research question: how can we achieve reliable and accurate automatic evaluation of model-generated content?

![Refer to caption](https://arxiv.org/html/x1.png)

Figure 1. Illustration of automatic evaluation for text, visual and speech generation.

Although human evaluation remains the gold standard for assessing content quality, its high cost and inherent non-reproducibility limit its scalability for large-scale applications (Lan et al., [2020](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib168), [2024d](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib171)). This has prompted researchers to develop automatic evaluation metrics that correlate strongly with human judgments (Li et al., [2024f](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib195), [b](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib181)). As shown in Figure [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#S1.F1 "Figure 1 ‣ 1. Introduction ‣ A Survey of Automatic Evaluation Methods on Text, Visual and Speech Generations"), automatic evaluation aims to assess model-generated content quality based on specific evaluation criteria, reference answers, and context using appropriate evaluation methods.

Despite this progress, the field lacks a systematic survey of current developments in automatic evaluation across different tasks and modalities. To address this gap, in this paper, we provide a comprehensive review and a unified taxonomy of automatic evaluation methods across text, visual, and speech modalities, offering insights into this evolving field. We begin with an in-depth analysis of automatic evaluation techniques in Natural Language Generation (NLG), which has seen the most significant advances (Tian et al., [2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib371); Li et al., [2024f](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib195), [b](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib181)). Specifically, we describe and analyze the attributations of existing automatic evaluation methods, and conduct a systematic meta-evaluation of existing automatic evaluation methods. Building on this analysis, we extend our review to other two important generative AI tasks: visual generation and audio generation. For each, we summarize the current development of automatic evaluation methods and outline promising directions for future research.

##### Difference from Related Surveys

Existing surveys on automatic evaluation techniques primarily focus on specific methodological approaches within NLG tasks, like LLM-based evaluation methods (Li et al., [2024f](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib195); Tian et al., [2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib371); Li et al., [2024b](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib181)). In contrast, our work provides a unified framework for automatic evaluation across three key modalities: text, visual, and speech. We cover the complete evolution of evaluation methods, from traditional heuristic approaches to modern LLM-based techniques. This cross-modal perspective offers a more comprehensive understanding of evaluation methodologies across generative AI systems.

## 2. Preliminary

In this section, we introduce the fundamental concepts of automatic evaluation methods (Section [2.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#S2.SS1 "2.1. Concepts for Evaluation ‣ 2. Preliminary ‣ A Survey of Automatic Evaluation Methods on Text, Visual and Speech Generations")), and then describe three mainstream evaluation protocols in Section [2.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#S2.SS2 "2.2. Evaluation Protocols ‣ 2. Preliminary ‣ A Survey of Automatic Evaluation Methods on Text, Visual and Speech Generations"): single-wise, pair-wise, and corpus-wise evaluation.

### 2.1. Concepts for Evaluation

As shown in Figure [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#S1.F1 "Figure 1 ‣ 1. Introduction ‣ A Survey of Automatic Evaluation Methods on Text, Visual and Speech Generations"), automatic evaluations require four key components: (1) Context; (2) Evaluation criteria; (3) Reference answer; and (4) Model-generated content to be evaluated.

##### Context ($`\mathbf{c}`$)

refers to the input information that models use to generate content. Examples include conversation history in dialogue generation tasks (Lan et al., [2024a](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib167)) and text prompts in text-to-image or text-to-video applications (Tu et al., [2024a](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib379); Yang et al., [2024b](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib442)).

##### Evaluation criteria ($`{{\mathbf{c}}{\mathbf{r}}{\mathbf{i}}}.`$)

comprise task-specific dimensions designed for assessment, such as fluency for open-domain text generation (Su et al., [2022](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib350); Fu et al., [2023a](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib72)) and coherence for text summarization (Fabbri et al., [2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib65)).

##### Reference answer ($`\mathbf{r}`$)

is widely used for robust evaluation in typical NLG tasks such as translation and summarization (Papineni et al., [2002](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib284); Lin, [2004](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib203)). However, relying on a single or limited number of reference answers makes it difficult to effectively cover the vast space of possible outputs in open-ended generation tasks (Lan et al., [2020](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib168)), leading to suboptimal evaluation. Consequently, reference-free evaluation methods have gained significant attention (Fu et al., [2023a](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib72)), as they do not require reference answers during evaluation. In contrast, methods that depend on reference answers are termed reference-based evaluation methods.

##### Generation ($`\mathbf{g}`$)

refers to the model-generated content being evaluated, including text, images, videos, and audio.

### 2.2. Evaluation Protocols

Unlike previous works (Li et al., [2024f](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib195)), we categorize existing automatic evaluation methods into three mainstream evaluation protocols: single-wise, pair-wise, and corpus-wise evaluation. These protocols are described below.

##### Single-Wise Evaluation

directly assesses the quality of one specific generation ($`g`$):

```math
{(r^{\ast},s)} = M_{\text{AE}}{(c^{\ast},cri.^{\ast},r^{\ast},g)}
```

where $`M_{\text{AE}}`$ represents any automatic evaluation method. $`r^{\ast}`$ is the textual rationale analyzing and describing the quality of $`g`$, typically generated by LLM-based evaluation methods (Zheng et al., [2023a](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib498)) (Section [3.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#S3.SS4 "3.4. LLM-based Evaluation ‣ 3. Automatic Evaluation for Neural Text Generation (NLG) ‣ A Survey of Automatic Evaluation Methods on Text, Visual and Speech Generations")). $`s`$ is a quality score reflecting the generation quality, usually expressed as a Likert Score (Zheng et al., [2023b](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib499)) within a constrained range, where higher scores indicate better quality. The context $`c`$, criteria $`{cri}.`$, and reference answer $`r`$ are optional depending on evaluation settings and tasks, hence marked with $`\ast`$.

##### Pair-wise Evaluation

is another important and widely-used protocol (Li et al., [2024e](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib187)) that determines preference between two generations ($`g_{A},g_{B}`$):

```math
{(r^{\ast},p)} = M_{\text{AE}}{(c^{\ast},cri.^{\ast},r^{\ast},g_{A},g_{B})}
```

Here, $`p`$ is the preference label indicating which generation is better. Compared to single-wise evaluation, pair-wise evaluation is more robust and objective (Li et al., [2024g](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib189)).

##### Corpus-level Evaluation

assesses the quality of all generations in a test set at the corpus level:

```math
s = M_{\text{AE}}{(c^{\ast},cri.^{\ast},r^{\ast},R,G)}
```

where $`R = {\{ r_{i}\}}_{i = 1}^{N}`$ and $`G = {\{ g_{i}\}}_{i = 1}^{N}`$ represent all $`N`$ references and model-generated samples in the corpus. Unlike single-wise and pair-wise protocols, most corpus-level evaluation methods do not generate explanatory rationales (Pillutla et al., [2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#bib.bib295)). Since corpus-level evaluation does not assess individual samples, it is considerably more coarse-grained than single-wise and pair-wise evaluation protocols.

As demonstrated in the right part of the Figure [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2506.10019v1#S1.F1 "Figure 1 ‣ 1. Introduction ‣ A Survey of Automatic Evaluation Methods on Text, Visual and Speech Generations"), a good automatic evaluation methods should correlates well with human judgments and the generated evaluation rationale should be effective, accurate and helpful.

## 3. Automatic Evaluation for Neural Text Generation (NLG)
